To encrypt the text, a Caesar cipher,,, the following steps:
1. Convert each letter of the plain text to its corresponding ASCII value.
2. Add the shift value (3 in this case) to each ASCII value.
3. Convert the resulting ASCII values back to their corresponding letters.

X ->  (ASCII value: 88) ->  (add 3) ->  (91) -> A
q -> (ASCII value:113) -> (add3) -> (116) -> r
y -> (ASCII value:121) -> (add3) -> (124) -> o
d -> (ASCII value:100) -> (add3) -> (103) -> f
U -> (ASCII value:85) -> (add3) -> (88) -> W
q -> (ASCII value:113) -> (add3) -> (116) -> r
z -> (ASCII value:122) -> (add3) -> (125) -> x
n -> (ASCII value:110) -> (add3) -> (113) -> p
S -> (ASCII value:83) -> (add3) -> (86) -> V
K -> (ASCII value:75) -> (add3) -> (78) -> O
! -> (ASCII value:33) -> (add3) -> (36) ->!
q -> (ASCII value:113) -> (add3) -> (116) -> r
y -> (ASCII value:121) -> (add3) -> (124) -> o
The resulting encrypted text is: Aro fWrozV O!ro
Note that this encryption method is case-sensitive, meaning that it preserves the case of the original text.

Record #7
  cipher_text: Encode the following text to a Caesar cipher. The shift is 9.
plain text: dXaotepf N kycFK Z!
The Caesar cipher is a type of substitution cipher in which each letter in the plaintext is 'shifted' a certain number of places down the alphabet. In this case, the shift is 9.
To encrypt the plaintext "dXaotepf N kycFK Z!", we need to shift each letter by 9 places:
* 'd' becomes 'r'
* 'X' becomes 'K'
* 'a' becomes 'h'
* 'o' becomes 'w'
* 't' becomes 'x'
* 'e' becomes 'l'
* 'p' becomes 'v'
* 'f' becomes 'm'
* ' ' (space) remains ' '
* 'N' becomes 'I'
* 'k' becomes 's'
* 'y' becomes 'b'
* 'c' becomes 'j'
* 'F' becomes 'E'
* 'K' becomes 'G'
* ' ' (space) remains ' '
* 'Z' becomes 'A'
* '!' becomes ','
So the Caesar cipher for the plaintext "dXaotepf N kycFK Z!" with a shift of 9 is "rKhlwxmv I sbeHG A,".

The Caesar cipher is a type of substitution cipher in which each letter in the plaintext is 'shifted' a certain number of places down the alphabet. In this case, the shift is 12.
To encrypt the plaintext "iFAveJIa Yqfcbg iPpMBr DrelHW qhodPO!" using a Caesar cipher with a shift of 12, we can follow these steps:
1. Identify the letters in the plaintext and their positions in the alphabet.
2. Shift each letter 12 places down the alphabet.
3. If a letter is shifted past the end of the alphabet, wrap around to the beginning.
For example, the letter 'i' is the ninth letter of the alphabet. If we shift it 12 places down, we get to the twenty-first letter, 'u'. The letter 'F' is the sixth letter of the alphabet. If we shift it 12 places down, we get to the eighteenth letter, 'S'.

encrypted text: rZWbzKLz Buvjde zSsmXq ZlqnRv!
Note that we have wrapped around to the beginning of the alphabet for the letters 'a' and 'p', which are shifted past 'z'.

The Caesar cipher is a type of substitution cipher in which each letter in the plaintext is 'shifted' a certain number of places down the alphabet. In this case, the shift is 12.
To encrypt the plaintext "oUQ xjUBpWm Amsw Yrgjbg C Fg?" using a Caesar cipher with a shift of 12, we can follow these steps:
1. Convert all letters to uppercase for consistency.
2. Shift each letter 12 places down the alphabet.
3. If a letter is shifted past the end of the alphabet, wrap around to the beginning.
4. Leave non-letter characters (such as spaces and punctuation) unchanged.
Applying these steps to the given plaintext, we get:
1. oUQ xjUBpWm Amsw Yrgjbg C Fg? -> OUQ XJUBPWM AMWS YRGJBG C FG?

	* ? -> ?

The Caesar cipher is a type of substitution cipher in which each letter in the plaintext is 'shifted' a certain number of places down the alphabet. In this case, the shift is 12.
To encrypt the plaintext "oRjRraIA BW C Ztyw RkOT sOEWOT yergn?" using a Caesar cipher with a shift of 12, we can follow these steps:
1. Identify the letters in the plaintext and their corresponding positions in the alphabet. For example, the letter 'o' is the 15th letter of the alphabet, 'R' is the 18th letter, and so on.
2. Shift each letter down the alphabet by the specified number of places. In this case, we will shift each letter down 12 places. So, for example, 'o' becomes 'a', 'R' becomes 'I', and so on.
3. If a letter is shifted past the end of the alphabet, wrap around to the beginning of the alphabet. For example, if we shift the letter 'z' down 12 places, it becomes 'a'.
4. Keep in mind that spaces, punctuation, and other non-alphabetic characters should be left unchanged.
